<p><b>Nancy Patricia D'Alesandro Pelosi</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born March 26, 1940) is an American politician who is the <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Party leaders of the United States House of Representatives">Minority Leader</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>, representing <a href="/wiki/California%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="California's 12th congressional district">California's 12th congressional district</a>. She previously served as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives#List_of_Speakers" title="List of Speakers of the United States House of Representatives">52nd</a> <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker of the United States House of Representatives</a> from 2007 to 2011, the only woman to do so, and is to date the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_line_of_succession#Current_order" title="United States presidential line of succession">highest-ranking</a> female politician in American history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>A member of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>, Pelosi represents <a href="/wiki/California%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="California's 12th congressional district">California's 12th congressional district</a>, which consists of four-fifths of the city and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">county of San Francisco</a>. The district was numbered as the <a href="/wiki/California%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="California's 5th congressional district">5th</a> during Pelosi's first three terms in the House, and as the <a href="/wiki/California%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="California's 8th congressional district">8th</a> from 1993 to 2013. She served as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Party_whips_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Party whips of the United States House of Representatives">House Minority Whip</a> from 2002 to 2003, and was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minority_Leader_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Minority Leader of the United States House of Representatives">House Minority Leader</a> from 2003 to 2007, holding the post during the <a href="/wiki/108th_United_States_Congress" title="108th United States Congress">108th</a> and <a href="/wiki/109th_United_States_Congress" title="109th United States Congress">109th Congresses</a> alongside President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. Pelosi is the first woman, the first Californian and first <a href="/wiki/Italian_Americans" title="Italian Americans">Italian-American</a> to lead a major party in Congress. After the Democrats took control of the House in 2007 and increased their majority in 2009, Pelosi was elected <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker of the House</a> for the <a href="/wiki/110th_United_States_Congress" title="110th United States Congress">110th</a> and <a href="/wiki/111th_United_States_Congress" title="111th United States Congress">111th Congresses</a> alongside Presidents <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a>.</p>
<p>On November 17, 2010, Pelosi was elected as the Democratic Leader by House Democrats and therefore the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minority_Leader" title="Minority Leader">Minority Leader</a> in the Republican-controlled House for the <a href="/wiki/112th_United_States_Congress" title="112th United States Congress">112th Congress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life.2C_education.2C_and_early_career">Early life, education, and early career</span></h2>
<p>Pelosi is Italian-American and was born <b>Nancy Patricia D'Alesandro</b> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, Maryland. She is the youngest of six children of Annunciata M. "Nancy" (née Lombardi), who was born in <a href="/wiki/Campobasso" title="Campobasso">Campobasso</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Italy" title="South Italy">South Italy</a>, on 25 March 1909, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_D%27Alesandro,_Jr." title="Thomas D'Alesandro, Jr.">Thomas D'Alesandro, Jr.</a>, who was a Democratic party U.S. Congressman from Maryland and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Baltimore" title="Mayor of Baltimore">Mayor of Baltimore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frelibrar_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-frelibrar-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Pelosi's brother, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_L._J._D%27Alesandro_III" title="Thomas L. J. D'Alesandro III">Thomas D'Alesandro III</a>, also a Democrat, was mayor of Baltimore from 1967 to 1971, when he chose not to run for re-election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi was involved with politics from an early age. In her outgoing remarks as the 60th Speaker of the House, Pelosi noted that she had been present at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inaugural_address_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Inaugural address of John F. Kennedy">inaugural address</a> as President in January 1961. She graduated from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Notre_Dame" title="Institute of Notre Dame">Institute of Notre Dame</a>, a Catholic all-girls high school in Baltimore, and from Trinity College (now <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Washington_University" title="Trinity Washington University">Trinity Washington University</a>) in Washington, D.C., in 1962 with a B.A. in <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Pelosi interned for Senator <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Brewster" title="Daniel Brewster">Daniel Brewster</a> (D-Maryland) alongside future House Majority Leader <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">Steny Hoyer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> She met Paul Frank Pelosi (b. April 15, 1940, in San Francisco)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> while she was attending Trinity College.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> They married in Baltimore at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Mary_Our_Queen" title="Cathedral of Mary Our Queen">Cathedral of Mary Our Queen</a> on September 7, 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> After the couple married, they moved to New York, and then to San Francisco in 1969, where Mr. Pelosi's brother, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Pelosi" title="Ron Pelosi">Ronald Pelosi</a>, was a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_and_County_of_San_Francisco" title="City and County of San Francisco">City and County of San Francisco</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Board_of_Supervisors" title="Board of Supervisors">Board of Supervisors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>After moving to San Francisco, Pelosi worked her way up in Democratic politics. She became a friend of one of the leaders of the California Democratic Party, 5th District Congressman <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Burton" title="Phillip Burton">Phillip Burton</a>.</p>
<p>In 1976, Pelosi was elected as a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Committee" title="Democratic National Committee">Democratic National Committee</a> member from California, a position she would hold until 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-13">[13]</a></sup> She was elected as party chair for Northern California on January 30, 1977, and for the <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">California Democratic Party</a>, which she held from 1981 until 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi was appointed Finance Chair of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Senatorial_Campaign_Committee" title="Democratic Senatorial Campaign Committee">Democratic Senatorial Campaign Committee</a>, the campaign arm of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate">U.S. Senate</a> Democrats, in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-13">[13]</a></sup> That same year, she ran to succeed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chuck_Manatt" title="Chuck Manatt">Chuck Manatt</a> as chair of the Democratic National Committee, but lost to then-DNC Treasurer <a href="/wiki/Paul_G._Kirk" title="Paul G. Kirk">Paul G. Kirk</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HotlineOnCall_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-HotlineOnCall-14">[14]</a></sup> Pelosi left her post as DSCC finance chair in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._House_of_Representatives">U.S. House of Representatives</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="373" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg/190px-Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg/285px-Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/44/Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_1993_congressional_photo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An early congressional photo of Pelosi taken in 1993.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Phillip Burton died in 1983 and was succeeded by his wife, <a href="/wiki/Sala_Burton" title="Sala Burton">Sala</a>. In late 1986, Sala became ill with cancer and decided not to run for reelection in 1988. She picked Pelosi as her designated successor, guaranteeing her the support of the Burtons' contacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationnewface_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-nationnewface-15">[15]</a></sup> Sala died on February 1, 1987, just a month after being sworn in for a second full term. Pelosi won the special election to succeed her, narrowly defeating San Francisco Supervisor <a href="/wiki/Harry_Britt" title="Harry Britt">Harry Britt</a> on April 7, 1987, then easily defeating Republican candidate Harriet Ross on June 2, 1987; Pelosi took office a week later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi represents one of the safest Democratic districts in the country. Democrats have held the seat since 1949 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republicans</a>, who currently make up only 13 percent of registered voters in the district, have not made a serious bid for the seat since the early 1960s. She won the seat in her own right in 1988 and has been reelected 10 more times with no substantive opposition, winning by an average of 80 percent of the vote. She has not participated in candidates' debates since her 1987 race against Harriet Ross.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The strongest challenge Pelosi has faced was in 2008 when anti-war activist <a href="/wiki/Cindy_Sheehan" title="Cindy Sheehan">Cindy Sheehan</a> polled 16% and Pelosi won with 72%.</p>
<p>She has the distinction of contributing the most among members of Congress to other congressional campaigns because she is in a safe district and does not need the campaign funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Committee_assignments">Committee assignments</span></h3>
<p>In the House, she served on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_Committee_on_Appropriations" title="U.S. House Committee on Appropriations">Appropriations</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_Permanent_Select_Committee_on_Intelligence" title="U.S. House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence">Intelligence</a> Committees, and was the ranking Democrat on the Intelligence Committee until her election as Minority Leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Speakership_career">Pre-Speakership career</span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Pelosi was elected the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_Minority_Whip" title="House Minority Whip">House Minority Whip</a>, second-in-command to Minority Leader <a href="/wiki/Dick_Gephardt" title="Dick Gephardt">Dick Gephardt</a> of <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>. She was the first woman in U.S. history to hold that post.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, after Gephardt resigned as minority leader to seek the Democratic nomination in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">2004 presidential election</a>, Pelosi was elected to replace him, becoming the first woman to lead a major party in the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Speaker_of_the_House">Speaker of the House</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomination">Nomination</span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_2006" title="United States House of Representatives elections, 2006">2006 Midterm Elections</a>, the Democrats took control of the House by picking up 31 seats. On November 16, 2006, Pelosi was unanimously chosen by her caucus as the Democratic candidate for Speaker, effectively making her Speaker-elect. While the Speaker is elected by the full House membership, in modern practice the election is a formality, since the Speaker always comes from the majority party.</p>
<p>Pelosi supported her longtime friend <a href="/wiki/John_Murtha" title="John Murtha">John Murtha</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> for the position of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_Majority_Leader" title="House Majority Leader">House Majority Leader</a>, the second-ranking post in the House Democratic caucus. His competitor was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_Minority_Whip" title="House Minority Whip">House Minority Whip</a> <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">Steny Hoyer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, who had been Pelosi's second-in-command since 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Pelosi and Hoyer had a somewhat frosty relationship dating back to 2001, when they ran against each other for minority whip. However, Hoyer was elected as House Majority Leader over Murtha by a margin of 149–86 within the caucus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 3, Pelosi defeated Republican <a href="/wiki/John_Boehner" title="John Boehner">John Boehner</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> with 233 votes compared to his 202 votes in the election for Speaker of the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> She was nominated by <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a> of <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, the incoming chairman of the House Democratic Caucus, and sworn in by her longtime friend <a href="/wiki/John_Dingell" title="John Dingell">John Dingell</a> of <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dean_of_the_House_of_Representatives" title="Dean of the House of Representatives">Dean of the House of Representatives</a> traditionally does.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="772" data-file-width="515" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg/220px-2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg/330px-2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg/440px-2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2007SOU_Bush_Cheney_Pelosi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi (right) with Vice President <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a> behind President George W. Bush at the <a href="/wiki/2007_State_of_the_Union_Address" title="2007 State of the Union Address">2007 State of the Union Address</a> making history as the first woman to sit behind the podium at such an address. President Bush acknowledged this by beginning his speech with the words, "Tonight, I have a high privilege and distinct honor of my own – as the first President to begin the State of the Union message with these words: Madam Speaker".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With her election, Pelosi became the first woman, the first Californian, and the first Italian-American to hold the Speakership. She is also the second Speaker from a state west of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The first was <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tom_Foley" title="Tom Foley">Tom Foley</a>, the last Democrat to hold the post before Pelosi.</p>
<p>During her speech, she discussed the historical importance of being the first female to hold the position of Speaker:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"This is a historic moment – for the Congress, and for the women of this country. It is a moment for which we have waited more than 200 years. Never losing faith, we waited through the many years of struggle to achieve our rights. But women weren't just waiting; women were working. Never losing faith, we worked to redeem the promise of America, that all men and women are created equal. For our daughters and granddaughters, today, we have broken the <a href="/wiki/Glass_ceiling" title="Glass ceiling">marble ceiling</a>. For our daughters and our granddaughters, the sky is the limit, anything is possible for them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110speech_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-110speech-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>She also spoke on Iraq as the major issue facing the 110th Congress, while incorporating some Democratic Party beliefs:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"The election of 2006 was a call to change – not merely to change the control of Congress, but for a new direction for our country. Nowhere were the American people more clear about the need for a new direction than in Iraq. The American people rejected an open-ended obligation to a war without end."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110speech_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-110speech-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenure">Tenure</span></h4>
<p>As Speaker, Pelosi was still the leader of the House Democrats; the Speaker is considered to be the leader of his or her House caucus. However, by tradition, she did not normally participate in debate and almost never voted on the floor (though she had every right to as a full House member). She was also not a member of any House committees.</p>
<p>Pelosi was re-elected Speaker in 2009.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> poll conducted in March 2010 found that 37% of registered voters have an unfavorable opinion of the speaker, with 11% approving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> According to a March 2010 <a href="/wiki/Rasmussen_Reports" title="Rasmussen Reports">Rasmussen</a> poll, 64% of voters nationally view the speaker unfavorably, and 29% have a favorable opinion of Pelosi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Social Security Mandate</dt>
</dl>
<p>Shortly after winning re-election, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> claimed a <a href="/wiki/Mandate_(politics)" title="Mandate (politics)">mandate</a> for an ambitious second-term agenda and proposed reforming <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> by allowing workers to redirect a portion of their Social Security withholding into stock and bond investments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Pelosi strongly opposed the plan, saying there was no crisis, and as minority leader she imposed intense party discipline on her caucus, leading them to near-unanimous opposition to Bush's proposal, and subsequent defeat of the proposed plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Blocking of impeachment proceedings against President Bush</dt>
</dl>
<p>In the wake of President George W. Bush's reelection in 2004, several leading House Democrats believed that Democrats should pursue <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movement_to_impeach_George_W._Bush" title="Movement to impeach George W. Bush">impeachment proceedings against the president</a>. They asserted that Bush had misled Congress about <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iraq_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Iraq and weapons of mass destruction">Iraq</a>, and had violated the civil liberties of Americans by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSA_warrantless_surveillance_controversy" title="NSA warrantless surveillance controversy">authorizing wiretaps without a warrant</a>.</p>
<p>In May 2006, with an eye on the upcoming congressional elections–which offered the possibility of Democrats taking back control of the House for the first time since 1994–Pelosi told colleagues that, while the Democrats would conduct vigorous oversight of Bush administration policy, an impeachment investigation was "off the table". (A week earlier, she had told the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> that, although Democrats would not set out to impeach the president, "you never know where" investigations might lead.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>After becoming Speaker of the House in January 2007, Pelosi held firm against impeachment, notwithstanding strong support for that course of action among constituents in her home district. In the November 2008 election, Pelosi withstood a challenge for her seat by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-war" title="Anti-war">anti-war</a> activist <a href="/wiki/Cindy_Sheehan" title="Cindy Sheehan">Cindy Sheehan</a>, who ran as an independent primarily because of Pelosi's refusal to pursue impeachment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>The "Hundred Hours"</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/100-Hour_Plan" title="100-Hour Plan">100-Hour Plan</a></div>
<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_elections,_2006" title="United States elections, 2006">U.S. 2006 midterm elections</a>, Pelosi announced a plan for action: If elected, she and the newly empowered Democratic caucus would push through most of its program during the first hundred hours of the 110th Congress' term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The origin for the name "first hundred hours" is a play on words derived from former Democratic <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>'s promise for quick action on the part of government (to combat the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>) during his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hundred_Days_Congress" title="Hundred Days Congress">"first hundred days"</a> in office. <a href="/wiki/Newt_Gingrich" title="Newt Gingrich">Newt Gingrich</a>, who became Speaker of the House in 1995, had a similar 100-day agenda to implement the <a href="/wiki/Contract_with_America" title="Contract with America">Contract with America</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Opposition to Iraq War troop surge of 2007</dt>
</dl>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War_troop_surge_of_2007" title="Iraq War troop surge of 2007">Iraq War troop surge of 2007</a></div>
<p>On January 5, 2007, reacting to suggestions from President Bush's confidantes that he would increase troop levels in Iraq (which he announced in a speech a few days later), Pelosi joined with Senate Majority Leader <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a> to condemn the plan. They sent Bush a letter saying, "[T]here is no purely military solution in Iraq. There is only a political solution. Adding more combat troops will only endanger more Americans and stretch our military to the breaking point for no strategic gain. ... Rather than deploy additional forces to Iraq, we believe the way forward is to begin the phased redeployment of our forces in the next four to six months, while shifting the principal mission of our forces there from combat to training, logistics, force protection and counter-terror."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>2008 Democratic National Convention</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg/200px-Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg/300px-Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg/400px-Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_DNC_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi conducts convention business during the first day of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, Colorado.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pelosi was named Permanent Chair of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, Colorado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Health Care Reform</dt>
</dl>
<p>Pelosi has been credited for spearheading <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama's</a> <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">health care law</a> when it seemed that it would go down in defeat. After Republican <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brown_(politician)" title="Scott Brown (politician)">Scott Brown</a> won Democratic <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Ted Kennedy</a>'s former senate seat in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_special_election_in_Massachusetts,_2010" title="United States Senate special election in Massachusetts, 2010">January 2010 Massachusetts special election</a> and thereby causing the Senate Democrats to lose their filibuster proof majority, Obama agreed with then chief of staff <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a>'s idea that he should do smaller initiatives that could pass easily. Pelosi, however, dismissed the president's fear and instead mocked his scaled-back ideas as "kiddie care."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> After convincing the president that this would be their only shot at health care because of the large Democratic majorities they currently had, she rallied her Democratic caucus as she began an "unbelievable marathon" of a two-month session to craft the health care bill, which successfully passed the House. In Obama's remarks before signing the bill into law, he specifically credited Pelosi as being "one of the best Speakers the House of Representatives has ever had."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-healthcarereform_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-healthcarereform-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Speakership_career">Post-Speakership career</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="654" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg/220px-Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg/330px-Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg/440px-Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Obama_meets_with_Congressional_Leadership_July_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> meets with Congressional Leadership, July 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though Pelosi was re-elected by a comfortable margin in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_2010" title="United States House of Representatives elections, 2010">2010 midterm elections</a>, the Democrats lost 63 seats and ceded control of the House of Representatives to the Republicans. Despite the electoral setback suffered by her party, Pelosi sought to continue leading the House Democratic Caucus in the position of Minority Leader, the office she held prior to becoming Speaker. After Pelosi's disparate intra-party opposition failed to pass a motion to delay the leadership vote,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Pelosi was elected Minority Leader for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/112th_Congress" title="112th Congress">112th Congress</a>. On November 14, 2012, Pelosi announced she would remain on as Democratic leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tim_Ryan_(politician)" title="Tim Ryan (politician)">Tim Ryan</a> initiated a bid to replace Pelosi as House Minority Leader on November 17, 2016, prompted by colleagues following the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016 presidential election</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> After Pelosi agreed to give more leadership opportunities to junior members,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> she defeated Ryan by a vote of 134-63 on November 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_insider_trading">Allegations of insider trading</span></h3>
<p>In November 2011, <a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a> alleged that Pelosi and several other member of Congress had used information they gleaned from closed sessions to make money on the stock market. The program cited Pelosi's purchases of Visa stock while a bill that would limit credit card fees was in the House. Pelosi denied the allegations and called the report "a right-wing smear."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> When the Stop Trading on Congressional Knowledge Act (or <a href="/wiki/STOCK_Act" title="STOCK Act">STOCK Act</a>) was introduced the next year, Pelosi voted for the bill and lauded its passing. Of Representatives <a href="/wiki/Louise_Slaughter" title="Louise Slaughter">Louise Slaughter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Walz" title="Tim Walz">Tim Walz</a>, who drafted the bill, Pelosi said they "shined a light on a gaping hole in our ethics laws and helped close it once and for all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_positions">Political positions</span></h2>
<p>Pelosi was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Progressive_Caucus" title="Congressional Progressive Caucus">Congressional Progressive Caucus</a>, but left in 2003 after being elected Minority Leader. Her longtime friend <a href="/wiki/Jim_McDermott" title="Jim McDermott">Jim McDermott</a> of Washington told <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> that he and other left-leaning Democratic congressmen sometimes wish that "she would tilt a little more our way from time to time". As Speaker, Pelosi has tried to focus more on economic than social issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In San Francisco, Pelosi has experienced conflicts with anti-war activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Nonetheless, she has never faced a serious challenger in the Democratic primary or from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_Party_USA" title="Green Party USA">Green Party</a>, which is competitive in local elections.</p>
<p>On September 2, 2008, she visited <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a>, Japan, for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> summit meeting of lower house speakers and offered flowers in <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima_Peace_Memorial_Park" title="Hiroshima Peace Memorial Park">Hiroshima Peace Memorial Park</a> for the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">1945 atomic bombing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1848" data-file-width="2784" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg/220px-Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg/330px-Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg/440px-Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_and_Wen_Jiabao.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi with <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Premier of the People's Republic of China">Chinese Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Wen_Jiabao" title="Wen Jiabao">Wen Jiabao</a> during a trip to China in 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On March 21, 2008, Pelosi criticized the People's Republic of China for its handling of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_unrest_in_Tibet" title="2008 unrest in Tibet">unrest in Tibet</a> and called on "freedom-loving people" worldwide to denounce China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn20mar2008_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn20mar2008-57">[57]</a></sup> She was quoted as saying, "The situation in Tibet is a challenge to the conscience of the world", while addressing a crowd of thousands of Tibetans in Dharamsala, India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn20mar2008_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn20mar2008-57">[57]</a></sup> She however did not call for a boycott of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> that were held in Beijing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>On October 24, 2008, Pelosi commended the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> for its "bold decision" to award the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakharov_Prize_for_Freedom_of_Thought" title="Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought">Sakharov Prize for Freedom of Thought</a> to <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_dissidents" title="List of Chinese dissidents">Chinese dissident</a> and human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Hu_Jia_(activist)" title="Hu Jia (activist)">Hu Jia</a>. Pelosi's statement read, "I call on the Chinese government to immediately and unconditionally release Hu Jia from prison and to respect the fundamental freedoms of all the people in China."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi publicly scolded Colombian President <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Uribe" title="Álvaro Uribe">Álvaro Uribe</a> during Uribe's May 2007 state trip to America. Pelosi met with Uribe and later released a statement that she and other members of Congress had "expressed growing concerns about the serious allegations" of links between Paramilitary groups and Colombian government officials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Pelosi also came out against the Colombian free trade agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba">Cuba</span></h3>
<p>In 2001, Pelosi voted in favor of keeping the travel restrictions on American citizens to Cuba, until the President has certified that Cuba has released all <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">political prisoners</a>, and extradited all individuals sought by the U.S. on charges of air piracy, drug trafficking and murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry,_Senators_McCain_and_Warner,_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi,_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1758" data-file-width="2643" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry%2C_Senators_McCain_and_Warner%2C_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi%2C_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry,_Senators_McCain_and_Warner,_House_Minority_Leader_Pelosi,_and_Representative_Engel_Chat_Before_Greeting_King_Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi before greeting the new King <a href="/wiki/Salman_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Salman of Saudi Arabia">Salman of Saudi Arabia</a>, Riyadh, January 2015. Saudi Arabia regards Iran as its main regional rival.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In a February 15, 2007, interview, Pelosi noted that Bush consistently said he supports a diplomatic resolution to differences with Iran "and I take him at his word". At the same time, she said, "I do believe that Congress should assert itself, though, and make it very clear that there is no previous authority for the president, any president, to go into Iran".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsMax_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewsMax-64">[64]</a></sup> On January 12, 2007, Congressman <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_B._Jones" title="Walter B. Jones">Walter B. Jones</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> introduced a resolution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> requiring that – absent a national emergency created by an attack, or a demonstrably imminent attack, by Iran upon the United States or its armed forces – the President must consult with Congress and receive specific authorization prior to initiating any use of military force against Iran.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> This resolution was removed from a military spending bill for the war in Iraq by Pelosi on March 13, 2007.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span></h3>
<p>In mid-October 2007, after the House Foreign Affairs Committee passed a resolution to label <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">the 1915 killing of Armenians by Ottoman Turks</a> as genocide, Pelosi pledged to bring the measure to a vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The draft resolution prompted warnings from President Bush and fierce criticism from Turkey, with Turkey's prime minister saying that approval of the resolution would endanger U.S.-Turkey relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> After House support eroded, the measure's sponsors dropped their call for a vote, and in late October Pelosi agreed to set the matter aside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_of_government_aircraft">Use of government aircraft</span></h3>
<p>In March 2009, the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a> wrote that the conservative watchdog group <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Watch" title="Judicial Watch">Judicial Watch</a> obtained emails sent by Pelosi's staff that requested that the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> (USAF) provide specific aircraft—a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a>—for Pelosi to use for taxpayer-funded travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Pelosi responded that the policy was initiated by President Bush due to post-<a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11</a> security concerns (Pelosi was third in line for <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_line_of_succession" title="United States presidential line of succession">presidential succession</a>) and was initially provided for the previous Speaker, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Hastert" title="Dennis Hastert">Dennis Hastert</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergeant_at_Arms" title="Sergeant at Arms">Sergeant at Arms</a> requested, for security reasons, that the plane provided be capable of non-stop flight, requiring a larger aircraft. The Pentagon said "no one has rendered judgment" that Pelosi's use of aircraft "is excessive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion">Abortion</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi voted against the <a href="/wiki/Partial-Birth_Abortion_Ban_Act" title="Partial-Birth Abortion Ban Act">Partial-Birth Abortion Ban Act</a> of 2003 and earlier attempts at similar bans, and voted against the criminalization of certain situations where a minor is transported across state lines for an abortion (HR 748, passed).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Project_Vote_Smart_Abortion_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Project_Vote_Smart_Abortion-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>She has voted in favor of lifting the ban on privately funded abortions at U.S. military facilities overseas (HA 209, rejected), in favor of an amendment that would repeal a provision that forbids service women and dependents from getting an abortion in overseas military hospitals (HA 722, rejected), in favor of stripping the prohibition of funding for organizations working overseas that uses its own funds to provide abortion services or engage in advocacy related to abortion services (HA 997, rejected). She also voted in favor of the 1998 Abortion Funding Amendment, which would have allowed the use of district funds to promote abortion-related activities, but would have prohibited the use of federal funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Project_Vote_Smart_Abortion_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Project_Vote_Smart_Abortion-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2009, Pelosi met with her <a href="/wiki/Bishop_(Catholic_Church)" title="Bishop (Catholic Church)">bishop</a>, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/George_Hugh_Niederauer" title="George Hugh Niederauer">George Hugh Niederauer</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_San_Francisco" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, and with <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> as a result of comments she made to <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brokaw" title="Tom Brokaw">Tom Brokaw</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Press" title="Meet the Press">Meet the Press</a></i> that many observers felt inaccurately portrayed <a href="/wiki/Catholic_theology" title="Catholic theology">Church teaching</a> on the subject of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_abortion" title="Catholic Church and abortion">abortion</a> and the beginning of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gun_laws">Gun laws</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi stands in favor of increased background checks for potential gun owners, as well as the controversial <a href="/wiki/Assault_weapons_legislation_in_the_United_States" title="Assault weapons legislation in the United States">banning</a> of <a href="/wiki/Assault_weapon" title="Assault weapon">assault weapons</a>. In February 2013, she called for the "Boldest possible move" on gun control, similar to a stance made just weeks earlier by former Representative, mass shooting victim and fellow gun control advocate, <a href="/wiki/Gabrielle_Giffords" title="Gabrielle Giffords">Gabrielle Giffords</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In 2012, she was given 0% ratings by both the <a href="/wiki/National_Rifle_Association" title="National Rifle Association">National Rifle Association</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gun_Owners_of_America" title="Gun Owners of America">Gun Owners of America</a> for her stances on gun control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a February, 2013, interview with <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a>, Pelosi misstated that gun ownership was protected by the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Amendment" title="First Amendment">First Amendment</a> addresses freedom of speech and the press, and it is the <a href="/wiki/Second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Second Amendment to the United States Constitution">Second Amendment</a> that addresses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gun_ownership" title="Gun ownership">gun ownership</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fiscal.2Fmonetary_policy">Fiscal/monetary policy</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi voted against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balanced_Budget_Amendment" title="Balanced Budget Amendment">1995 Balanced Budget Proposed Constitutional Amendment</a>, which was passed by the House by a 300–132 vote, but in the Senate fell two votes short of the 2/3 supermajority required (with 65 out of 100 Senators voting in favor).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoteSma4_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-VoteSma4-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>As Speaker of the House, she also spearheaded the <a href="/wiki/Fair_Minimum_Wage_Act_of_2007" title="Fair Minimum Wage Act of 2007">Fair Minimum Wage Act of 2007</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/100-Hour_Plan" title="100-Hour Plan">100-Hour Plan</a>. The Act raises the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a> in the United States and the territories of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Marianas_Islands" title="Northern Marianas Islands">Northern Marianas Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. American Samoa was initially absent from the act, but as part of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HR_2206" title="HR 2206">HR 2206</a> it was included. One Republican congressman who voted against the initial bill accused Pelosi of unethically benefiting <a href="/wiki/Del_Monte_Foods" title="Del Monte Foods">Del Monte Foods</a> (headquartered in her district) by the exclusion of the territory, where Del Monte's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/StarKist_Tuna" title="StarKist Tuna">StarKist Tuna</a> brand is a major employer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Pelosi co-sponsored legislation that omitted American Samoa from a raise in the minimum wage as early as 1999, prior to Del Monte's acquisition of StarKist Tuna in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> As of the 2002, 2004, and 2006 election cycles, Del Monte has not contributed to Democratic candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi opposed the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_reform" title="Welfare reform">welfare reform</a> proposed by President Bush as well as reforms proposed and passed under President Clinton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opinionjournal.com_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-opinionjournal.com-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_liberties">Civil liberties</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ellison-20070104.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2100" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ellison-20070104.jpg/220px-Ellison-20070104.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ellison-20070104.jpg/330px-Ellison-20070104.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ellison-20070104.jpg/440px-Ellison-20070104.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ellison-20070104.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Ellison" title="Keith Ellison">Keith Ellison</a> (right) at his swearing-in ceremony with <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a>'s Congressional Scorecard has given Pelosi a lifetime rating of 92% for her voting record on civil liberties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In 2001, she voted in favor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_Patriot_Act" title="USA Patriot Act">USA Patriot Act</a>, but voted against reauthorization of certain provisions in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> She voted against a <a href="/wiki/Flag_Desecration_Amendment" title="Flag Desecration Amendment">Constitutional amendment banning flag-burning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contraception">Contraception</span></h3>
<p>In a January 25, 2009, interview with <a href="/wiki/George_Stephanopoulos" title="George Stephanopoulos">George Stephanopoulos</a> for <a href="/wiki/ABC_News" title="ABC News">ABC News</a>, Pelosi said, "Well, the family planning services reduce cost. They reduce cost. The states are in terrible fiscal budget crises now and part of what we do for children's health, education and some of those elements are to help the states meet their financial needs. One of those – one of the initiatives you mentioned, the contraception, will reduce costs to the states and to the federal government."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<p>In 1999, Pelosi voted against the Ten Commandments being displayed in public buildings, including schools<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Pelosi voted for the <a href="/wiki/No_Child_Left_Behind_Act" title="No Child Left Behind Act">No Child Left Behind Act</a>, which instituted testing to track students' progress and authorized an increase in overall education spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoteSma7_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-VoteSma7-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="514" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg/220px-Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg/330px-Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg/440px-Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bush_and_Pelosi_at_Tuskegee_Airmen_ceremony.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and Pelosi honor 300 <a href="/wiki/Tuskegee_Airmen" title="Tuskegee Airmen">Tuskegee Airmen</a> at the Capitol building, March 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pelosi has supported the development of new technologies to reduce U.S. dependence upon foreign oil and remediate the adverse environmental effects of burning fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoteSma8_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-VoteSma8-93">[93]</a></sup> Pelosi has widely supported conservation programs and energy research appropriations. She has also voted to remove an amendment that would allow for oil and gas exploration in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Arctic National Wildlife Refuge">Arctic National Wildlife Refuge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoteSma9_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-VoteSma9-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi has blocked efforts to revive offshore oil drilling in protected areas, reasoning that <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore drilling</a> could lead to an increase in dependence on fossil fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span></h3>
<p>Speaker Pelosi was instrumental in the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a> of 2010. Pelosi was a key figure in convincing President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> to continue pushing for health care reform after the election of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Sen.</a> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brown_(politician)" title="Scott Brown (politician)">Scott Brown</a> in a January <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_election" title="Special election">special election</a>, a defeat that was seen as potentially fatal to Democratic reform efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-healthcarereform_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-healthcarereform-41">[41]</a></sup> After delivering 219 votes in the House for Obama's signature health care package, Pelosi was both praised and heckled as she made her way to Capitol Hill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelosi has voted to increase <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicaid" title="Medicaid">Medicaid</a> benefits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoteSma14_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-VoteSma14-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2332" data-file-width="3504" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg/220px-Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg/330px-Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg/440px-Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_060211.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pelosi at San Francisco's <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> Festival</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi voted against the <a href="/wiki/Secure_Fence_Act_of_2006" title="Secure Fence Act of 2006">Secure Fence Act of 2006</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq_War">Iraq War</span></h3>
<p>In 2002, Pelosi opposed the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Resolution" title="Iraq Resolution">Iraq Resolution</a> authorizing President Bush to use military force against Iraq,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HouseClerk_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-HouseClerk-99">[99]</a></sup> while stating that Iraq, like "other countries of concern", had WMDs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-House2_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-House2-100">[100]</a></sup> In explaining her opposition to the resolution, Pelosi noted that <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> Director <a href="/wiki/George_Tenet" title="George Tenet">George Tenet</a> had told Congress that the likelihood of Iraq's <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> launching an attack on the U.S. using weapons of mass destruction was low. "This is about the Constitution", Pelosi said. "It is about this Congress asserting its right to declare war when we are fully aware what the challenges are to us. It is about respecting the United Nations and a multilateral approach, which is safer for our troops." Despite Pelosi's opposition, Congress still passed a resolution authorizing President Bush to use the Armed Forces of the United States against Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi reaffirms that "America and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> share an unbreakable bond: in peace and war; and in prosperity and in hardship".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onIsrael_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-onIsrael-102">[102]</a></sup> Pelosi emphasized that "a strong relationship between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israel_%E2%80%93_United_States_relations" title="Israel – United States relations">United States and Israel</a> has long been supported by both Democrats and Republicans. America's commitment to the safety and security of the State of Israel is unwavering,...[h]owever, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_in_Iraq" title="War in Iraq">war in Iraq</a> has made both America and Israel less safe." Pelosi's voting record shows consistent support for Israel. Prior to 2006 elections in the Palestinian Authority, she voted for a Congressional initiative disapproving of participation in the elections by <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> and other organizations defined as terrorist by the legislation. She agrees with the current U.S. stance in support of land-for-peace. She has applauded Israeli "hopeful signs" of offering land, while criticizing Palestinian "threats" of not demonstrating peace in turn. She states, "If the Palestinians agree to coordinate with Israel on the evacuation, establish the rule of law, and demonstrate a capacity to govern, the world may be convinced that finally there is a real partner for peace".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onIsrael_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-onIsrael-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a>, Pelosi voted in favor of Resolution 921 on the count that "the seizure of Israeli soldiers by <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> terrorists was an unprovoked attack and Israel has the right, and indeed the obligation, to respond". She argues that organizations and political bodies in the Mideast like <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> "have a greater interest in maintaining a state of hostility with Israel than in improving the lives of the people they claim to represent". Pelosi asserts that civilians on both sides of the border "have been put at risk by the aggression of Hamas and Hezbollah" in part for their use of "civilians as shields by concealing weapons in civilian areas".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2008, Pelosi hosted a reception in Washington with Israeli <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> speaker <a href="/wiki/Dalia_Itzik" title="Dalia Itzik">Dalia Itzik</a>, along with 20 members of Congress, where they toasted the "strong friendship" between Israel and the United States. During the ceremony, Pelosi held up the replica dog tags of the three Israeli soldiers captured by Hezbollah and Hamas in 2006 and stated that she keeps them as a "symbol of the sacrifices made, sacrifices far too great by the people of the state of Israel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Gulf_War">First Gulf War</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi opposed U.S. intervention in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_Gulf_War" title="1991 Gulf War">1991 Gulf War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opinionjournal.com_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-opinionjournal.com-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_(9179648593).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg/220px-Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg/330px-Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg/440px-Nancy_Pelosi_%289179648593%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nancy_Pelosi_(9179648593).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 2013 <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Pride" title="San Francisco Pride">San Francisco Pride</a> Festival</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pelosi received a 100% rating from the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a> for the <a href="/wiki/107th_United_States_Congress" title="107th United States Congress">107th</a>, <a href="/wiki/108th_United_States_Congress" title="108th United States Congress">108th</a>, and <a href="/wiki/109th_United_States_Congress" title="109th United States Congress">109th</a> sessions of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>, indicating that she voted in agreement with HRC's slate of pro-gay legislative issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In 1996 she voted against the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and in 2004 and 2006, she voted against the proposed <a href="/wiki/Federal_Marriage_Amendment" title="Federal Marriage Amendment">Federal Marriage Amendment</a>, which would amend the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a> to define marriage federally as being between one man and one woman, thereby overriding states' individual rights to legalize <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_marriage" title="Gay marriage">gay marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> When the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a> overturned the <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_22_(2000)" title="California Proposition 22 (2000)">state's ban on same-sex marriage</a>, Pelosi released a statement welcoming the "historic decision." She voiced her opposition to <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8_(2008)" title="California Proposition 8 (2008)">Proposition 8</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_state_elections,_November_2008" title="California state elections, November 2008">successful ballot initiative</a>, which defined marriage in California as a union between one man and one woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Pelosi states that her <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> faith is behind her position on LGBT rights such as same-sex marriage: "My religion compels me—and I love it for it—to be against discrimination of any kind in our country, and I consider [the ban on gay marriage] a form of discrimination. I think it’s unconstitutional on top of that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marijuana_legalization">Marijuana legalization</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi supports <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legality_of_cannabis_in_the_United_States" title="Legality of cannabis in the United States">reform in marijuana laws</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> She also supports use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_marijuana" title="Medical marijuana">medical marijuana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_draft">Military draft</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bush,_Pelosi,_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House,_Nov_9,_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="342" data-file-width="514" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg/220px-Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg/330px-Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg/440px-Bush%2C_Pelosi%2C_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House%2C_Nov_9%2C_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bush,_Pelosi,_and_Hoyer_meeting_at_White_House,_Nov_9,_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Speaker-designate Pelosi and House Minority Whip <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">Steny Hoyer</a> meeting with <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> on November 9, 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In regard to Representative <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rangel" title="Charles Rangel">Charles Rangel</a>'s (D-NY) plan to introduce legislation that would reinstate the draft, Pelosi stated that she did not support such legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NSA_Spying.2FPRISM_Program">NSA Spying/PRISM Program</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi supports the Bush/Obama NSA spying program called <a href="/wiki/PRISM_(surveillance_program)" title="PRISM (surveillance program)">PRISM</a>. On June 22, 2013 she was booed at <a href="/wiki/Netroots_Nation" title="Netroots Nation">Netroots Nation</a> for saying <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> was a criminal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">Syria</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi supports the <a href="/wiki/Syria_Accountability_Act" title="Syria Accountability Act">Syria Accountability Act</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran_Freedom_and_Support_Act" title="Iran Freedom and Support Act">Iran Freedom and Support Act</a>. In a speech at the <a href="/wiki/American_Israel_Public_Affairs_Committee" title="American Israel Public Affairs Committee">AIPAC</a> 2005 annual conference, Pelosi said that "for too long, leaders from both parties haven't done enough" to put pressure on <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and China who are providing <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> with technological information on nuclear issues and missiles. "If evidence of participation by other nations in Iran's nuclear program is discovered, I will insist that the Administration use, rather than ignore, the evidence in determining how the U.S. deals with that nation or nations on other issues."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In April 2007, she visited <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a> and stated there "the road to Damascus is a road to peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liz15apr_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-liz15apr-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterboarding">Waterboarding</span></h3>
<p>Pelosi has stated that she now opposes the interrogation technique of <a href="/wiki/Waterboarding" title="Waterboarding">waterboarding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Hero_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Hero-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the CIA, while Pelosi was the <a href="/wiki/Ranking_member" title="Ranking member">ranking member</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_Intelligence_Committee" title="House Intelligence Committee">House Intelligence Committee</a>, she was briefed on the ongoing use of so-called "<a href="/wiki/Enhanced_interrogation_techniques" title="Enhanced interrogation techniques">enhanced interrogation techniques</a>", including waterboarding authorized for a captured terrorist, Abu Zubaydah,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_tude_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-post_tude-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> in one hour-long briefing in 2002. After the briefing, Pelosi said she "was assured by lawyers with the CIA and the Department of Justice that the methods were legal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Two unnamed former <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">Bush Administration</a> officials say that the briefing was detailed and graphic, and at the time she didn't raise substantial objections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterboarding_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-waterboarding-123">[123]</a></sup> One unnamed U.S. official present during the early briefings said, "In fairness, the environment was different then because we were closer to <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11</a> and people were still in a panic. But there was no objecting, no hand-wringing. The attitude was, 'We don't care what you do to those guys as long as you get the information you need to protect the American people.' "<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, several top Democratic lawmakers in the House signed a letter on June 26, 2009, alleging that <a href="/wiki/Director_of_the_Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Director of the Central Intelligence Agency">CIA Director</a> <a href="/wiki/Leon_Panetta" title="Leon Panetta">Leon Panetta</a> had asserted that the CIA misled Congress for a "number of years" spanning back to 2001, casting clouds on the controversy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Neither letter, lawmakers or the CIA provided details and the circumstances surrounding the allegations make it hard to assess the claims and counterclaims of both sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Democratic_Letter_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Democratic_Letter-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Officials in Congress say her ability to challenge the practices may have been hampered by strict rules of secrecy that prohibited her from being able to take notes or consult legal experts or members of her own staffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In an April 2009 press conference, Pelosi stated, "In that or any other briefing...we were not, and I repeat, were not told that waterboarding or any of these other enhanced interrogation techniques were used. What they did tell us is that they had some legislative counsel – the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Office_of_Legal_Council" title="Office of Legal Council">Office of Legislative Counsel</a> opinions that they could be used, but not that they would.
